"46 apples were in the basket . 22 are red and the rest are green . how many apples are green ?" ; "Sure, let's solve this problem step by step using calculations with << symbols.

Step 1: Start with the total number of apples in the basket, which is 46.

>>Total\ apples = 46<<

Step 2: We know that 22 of these apples are red, so we need to find out how many are green. To do that, we'll subtract the number of red apples from the total number of apples.

>>Green\ apples = Total\ apples - Red\ apples<<
>>Green\ apples = 46 - 22<<

Step 3: Calculate the number of green apples.

>>Green\ apples = 24$

So, there are 24 green apples in the basket.

What fraction of the students in the band are in either the trumpet section or the trombone section ?" ; "To find the fraction of students in the band who are in either the trumpet section or the trombone section, we need to add the fractions representing the students in each section and then subtract the overlap (students who are in both sections) to avoid counting them twice.

Fraction of students in the trumpet section: \(0.5\)

Fraction of students in the trombone section: \(0.125\)

Now, we add the fractions:

\(0.5 + 0.125 = 0.625\)

This represents the total fraction of students in either the trumpet section or the trombone section.

However, we need to subtract the overlap. To do this, we find the fraction of students who are in both sections. 

Since \(0.5\) of the students are in the trumpet section and \(0.125\) are in the trombone section, we can find the overlap by multiplying these fractions:

Overlap fraction: \(0.5 * 0.125 = 0.0625\)

Now, subtract the overlap from the total fraction:

\(0.625 - 0.0625 = 0.5625\)

Given that each section of the orchard produces 45 sacks of apples daily, and there are 8 sections in total, we can calculate the total number of sacks harvested each day by multiplying the number of sacks per section by the number of sections.

Number of sacks per section = 45
Number of sections = 8

Total number of sacks harvested daily = Number of sacks per section * Number of sections

Total number of sacks harvested daily = 45 * 8

Next, we need to calculate the number of apples in each sack. Since the question does not provide this information, we will assume a value for the number of apples in each sack. Let's assume there are 50 apples in each sack.

Number of apples in each sack = 50

To find the total number of apples harvested daily, we need to multiply the total number of sacks harvested daily by the number of apples in each sack.

Total number of apples harvested daily = Total number of sacks harvested daily * Number of apples in each sack

Total number of apples harvested daily = (45 * 8) * 50

Now we can calculate the total number of apples harvested every day.

Total number of apples harvested daily = 360 * 50
Total number of apples harvested daily = 18000

Therefore, the number of apples harvested every day is 18000.

"an online toy store stocked some toys . it sold 38 toys at the first week and 26 toys at the second week . if it had 19 toys left how many toys were in stock at the beginning ?" ; "Let's denote the number of toys in stock at the beginning as ""x"".

In the first week, the store sold 38 toys, so the number of toys remaining in stock is ""x - 38"".

In the second week, the store sold an additional 26 toys, so the number of toys remaining in stock is ""(x - 38) - 26"".

Given that there were 19 toys left, we can set up the equation:

(x - 38) - 26 = 19

Simplifying the equation:

x - 38 - 26 = 19

x - 64 = 19

Adding 64 to both sides of the equation:

x - 64 + 64 = 19 + 64

x = 83

Therefore, there were 83 toys in stock at the beginning.

Next, we are told that Doug lost 8 of his marbles at the playground. So, Doug would then have x - 8 marbles.

The worm climbs 8 inches and then slides back 3 inches every day.

"maura collects seashells every summer . her family stays at the beach house for 21 days . this summer maura found 75 seashells . she gave some to her little sister . maura then had 57 seashells . how many seashells did maura give to her sister ?" ; "Let's denote the number of seashells Maura gave to her sister as ""x"". 

We know that Maura found 75 seashells initially and gave some to her sister. After giving some to her sister, she had 57 seashells left. 

So, we can write the equation: 75 - x = 57.

To find the value of ""x"", we can solve this equation.

Starting with 75, subtracting x from both sides of the equation gives us: 75 - x - x = 57 - x.

Simplifying the equation gives us: 75 - 2x = 57.

To isolate the variable, we subtract 75 from both sides of the equation: 75 - 2x - 75 = 57 - 75.

Simplifying the equation gives us: -2x = -18.

Finally, to solve for ""x"", we divide both sides of the equation by -2: (-2x) / -2 = (-18) / -2.

Simplifying the equation gives us: x = 9.

Therefore, Maura gave 9 seashells to her sister.

"the central city zoo has 45 chimpanzees . every day the chimps eat a total of 72 bananas . next week the zoo is moving 18 chimps to a new cage . how many chimps will stay in the old cage ?" ; "Let's start by finding out how many bananas each chimp eats per day. To do this, we divide the total number of bananas by the number of chimps.

Total bananas per day = 72
Number of chimps = 45

So, bananas per chimp per day = Total bananas per day / Number of chimps

Bananas per chimp per day = 72 / 45 = 1.6 bananas

Next, let's find out how many bananas the 18 chimps that are being moved eat per day. We can do this by multiplying the number of bananas per chimp per day by the number of chimps being moved.

Bananas per chimp per day = 1.6 bananas
Number of chimps being moved = 18

Bananas eaten by the chimps being moved per day = Bananas per chimp per day * Number of chimps being moved

Bananas eaten by the chimps being moved per day = 1.6 * 18 = 28.8 bananas

Now, let's find out how many bananas the remaining chimps in the old cage eat per day. We can do this by subtracting the bananas eaten by the chimps being moved per day from the total bananas per day.

Total bananas per day = 72 bananas
Bananas eaten by the chimps being moved per day = 28.8 bananas

Bananas eaten by the remaining chimps per day = Total bananas per day - Bananas eaten by the chimps being moved per day

Bananas eaten by the remaining chimps per day = 72 - 28.8 = 43.2 bananas

Since each chimp eats 1.6 bananas per day, we can find out how many chimps will stay in the old cage by dividing the bananas eaten by the remaining chimps per day by the number of bananas per chimp per day.

Bananas eaten by the remaining chimps per day = 43.2 bananas
Bananas per chimp per day = 1.6 bananas

Number of chimps staying in the old cage = Bananas eaten by the remaining chimps per day / Bananas per chimp per day

Number of chimps staying in the old cage = 43.2 / 1.6 = 27

Therefore, 27 chimps will stay in the old cage.####

According to the information given, JT lost 14 cards, so the number of cards remaining after losing 14 is ""x - 14"". 

Next, JT gave 19 cards to his best friend, so the number of cards remaining after giving away 19 is ""(x - 14) - 19"".

Finally, it is mentioned that JT has 45 cards left, so we can set up the equation:

(x - 14) - 19 = 45

Simplifying the equation, we combine like terms:

x - 14 - 19 = 45
x - 33 = 45

To isolate the variable, we add 33 to both sides of the equation:

x - 33 + 33 = 45 + 33
x = 78

Therefore, JT had 78 cards at first.

11 + 6(P - 1) = 41

11 + 6P - 6 = 41

6P = 41 - 11 + 6

6P = 36

Finally, divide both sides by 6 to find the number of players (P):

P = 36 / 6

P = 6

So, there were 6 players on Paige's team.

Let's denote the number of people at the first concert as <<F>> and the number of people at the second concert as <<S>>. We know that the total number of people who attended both concerts is 65,899.

So, we can write the equation:
F + S = <<F + S = 65,899>> 65,899

We also know that the second concert had 119 more people in attendance than the first concert, so we can write another equation:
S = <<S = F + 119>> F + 119

Now we can use these two equations to solve for the number of people at the second concert. First, we'll substitute the second equation into the first one:

F + (F + 119) = <<F + (F + 119) = 65,899>> 65,899

Now, we can combine the terms:

2F + 119 = <<2F + 119 = 65,899>> 65,899

Subtract 119 from both sides to isolate 2F:

2F = <<2F = 65,899 - 119>> 65,899 - 119

2F = <<2F = 65,780>> 65,780

Now, divide by 2 to find the number of people at the first concert, F:

F = <<F = 6 / 5,780}2>> 6 / 5,780}2

Now, calculate F:

F = <<F = 32,890>> 32,890

S = <<S = F + 119>> F + 119

S = <<S = 32,890 + 119>> 32,890 + 119

S = <<S = 33,009>> 33,009

So, there were 33,009 people at the second concert.

Initial number of toys - 6 + 9 = 43

Subtract 6 from both sides of the equation:

Initial number of toys + 9 = 43 + 6

Initial number of toys + 9 = 49

Subtract 9 from both sides of the equation to find the initial number of toys:

Initial number of toys = 49 - 9

Initial number of toys = 40

So, Blithe initially had 40 toys.

"there are some passengers on a bus . at a bus stop 7 more passengers got on the bus and 9 passengers got off . if there are 26 passengers in the bus in the end how many passengers were there at first ?" ; "Let's start by considering the initial number of passengers on the bus as ""x"". 

After 7 more passengers got on the bus, the total number of passengers increased by 7 to become ""x + 7"".

Then, 9 passengers got off the bus, which means the total number of passengers decreased by 9 to become ""(x + 7) - 9"".

Finally, we know that in the end there are 26 passengers on the bus, so we can set up the equation:

""(x + 7) - 9 = 26""

Now, let's solve this equation step by step:

(x + 7) - 9 = 26
x + 7 - 9 = 26
x - 2 = 26
x = 26 + 2
x = 28

Therefore, there were 28 passengers on the bus initially.

We are given that Bruno had 39 books after his dad gave him the books, so we can set up the equation:

x - 4 + 10 = 39

x + 6 = 39

Therefore, Bruno had 33 books at first.

Number of yellow lights: 37
